The quantity of seawater used must be the maximum possible so as to minimise the drop in ph.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><br />\n</div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><span style=\"color: #333333; font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\">Once sea water cleaning is started than under no circumstances the washing should stop till the tank is cleaned. The final rinsing after seawater should be carried out with fresh water. There should be no possibility of leaving sea water for long periods static in contact with stainless steel. The sea water temperature should not be kept higher than 50C. It is important that there are no stagnant salt water pockets in pipelines. There can be no pitting if salt water flow is greater than 1.2 mtrs/ sec.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><br />\n</div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><span style=\"color: #333333; font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\">Always clean SS tanks asap after discharge even if the same chemical has to be loaded again and again.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><br />\n</div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><span style=\"color: #333333; font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\">In order to obtain the optimum corrosion resistance from stainless steel cargo tanks it is necessary to avoid damage to the tank surfaces. This can be achieved by care in design and fabrication and by treating the steel surface after fabrication in such a way to remove surface contamination.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><br />\n</div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><span style=\"color: #333333; font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\">Care in service should aim at retaining the passive layer on the steel surface which will than provide corrosion resistance throughout the life of the ship. Great care and right procedure should be used for tank cleaning especially after discharging corrosive cargoes like phosphoric acid and using sea water as initial cleaning medium.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><br />\n</div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><span style=\"color: #333333; font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\">Chemicals which attack stainless :<o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><span style=\"color: #333333; font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\">There is a full lloyds list available with this manual. Some corrode with impurities over the acceptable limit , some corrode due to temperatures over the acceptable limit. A few examples just for understanding are\u2014<o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><br />\n</div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><span style=\"color: #333333; font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\">Benzene sulphonyl chloride<o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><span style=\"color: #333333; font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\">Calcium hypochlorite<o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><span style=\"color: #333333; font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\">Chlorinated paraffins<o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><span style=\"color: #333333; font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\">Chlorobenzene ( benzyl chloride )<o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><span style=\"color: #333333; font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\">Dichloro benzene<o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><span style=\"color: #333333; font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\">Chlorohydrin<o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><span style=\"color: #333333; font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\">Chlorotoluene<o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><span style=\"color: #333333; font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\">Dischloroethane<o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><span style=\"color: #333333; font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\">Dichlorohexane<o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><span style=\"color: #333333; font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\">Dichloropropane<o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><span style=\"color: #333333; font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\">Epichlorohydrin<o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><span style=\"color: #333333; font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\">Drilling brines like calcium bromide and cal chloride soln<o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><span style=\"color: #333333; font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\">EDC<o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><span style=\"color: #333333; font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\">Formic acid<o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><span style=\"color: #333333; font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\">Lignin sulphonic acid<o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><span style=\"color: #333333; font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\">Magnesium chloride<o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><span style=\"color: #333333; font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\">Sodium salt solution ( sodium hydrate )<o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><span style=\"color: #333333; font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\">Perchloroethylene<o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><span style=\"color: #333333; font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\">Potassium chloride (&gt;10%)<o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><span style=\"color: #333333; font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\">Potassium hydroxide<o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><span style=\"color: #333333; font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\">Propionic acid<o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><span style=\"color: #333333; font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\">Sodium chlorate<o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><span style=\"color: #333333; font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\">Sodium nitrite sodium sulphate<o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><span style=\"color: #333333; font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\">Tetrachloro ethane<o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><span style=\"color: #333333; font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\">Trichloroethane trichloroethylene<o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><span style=\"color: #333333; font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\">Urea<o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><br />\n</div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><br />\n</div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><span style=\"color: #333333; font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\">Do not accept odd commercial name cargoes unless you know the product. Many times such things are done to beat the system for lesser customs duties, flouting Marpol laws etc. Read cargo specs carefully. Add up the percentages to form 100% . If does not add up find out what is missing. Of if some important component corrosion accelerators like chloride or flourides are missing from green/ black phosphoric specs find out why they are deliberately omitted.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><br />\n</div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><span style=\"color: #333333; font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\">Or if the moisture content of Epichlorohydrin is not mentioned find out why. For once the stainless steel has pitted you are responsible for destroying a good tank. Once pitting starts you cannot carry sensitive cargoes like potable Ethanol or HMD. Follow proper sampling procedures. Keep samples safely. If tank gets severely pitted get it analysed in an independent lab in order to challenge the false quality certificate. If the tank inspector challenges the condition of the SS cargo tank, counter challenge him by cleaning off part of the bulkhead where ever he wants with the product to be loaded to prove all is OK.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><br />\n</div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><span style=\"color: #333333; font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\">If Hypochlorite solutions are used for tank cleaning they must never be left in the slop tanks. Bleach or Sodium Hypochlorite (11 -13%) is very aggressive to SS especially at elevated temperatures.they must never be allowed to dry up on bulkheads.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><br />\n</div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><span style=\"color: #333333; font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\">Kosher Acetic acid is usually loaded only in stainless steel tanks, though it pits and causes inter granular corrosion.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><br />\n</div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><span style=\"color: #333333; font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\">Sludge sediment from Phosphoric acid made by the wet process ( Silica Quartz) accelerates corrosion. This is the reason why recirc is done.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><br />\n</div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><br />\n</div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><span style=\"color: #333333; font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\">You are not allowed to ballast stainless steel cargo tanks without taking permission from the EMS chemical operator. If it is necessary to ballast stainless steel tanks\u2014<o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><span style=\"color: #333333; font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\">1) Use clean water up to 98% .<o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><span style=\"color: #333333; font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\">2) Raise pH value of ballast from 8 to 11 using Caustic Potash.. Say put 40 kg KOH flakes in 1000 tons sea water.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><span style=\"color: #333333; font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\">3) Recirc<o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><span style=\"color: #333333; font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\">4) Short duration only.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><span style=\"color: #333333; font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\">As soon as the ballast is out rinse with fresh water.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><br />\n</div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><span style=\"color: #333333; font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\">After aggressive cargoes like Sulphuric acid preferably the initial quenching should be done with fresh water. Sulphuric acid leaves liquid top surface profile ( wedge ) of exhothermic corrosion. If it cannot be done immediately use nitrogen blanket. After dischg black/ green phosphoric prewash should preferably be with fresh water. If sufficient fresh water is not available at least the first and last wash can be with FW, with the salt not being allowed to dry up. Acidic stagnant sea water is very dangerous for SS. Weld spatter areas are corrosion initiation points. Weld spatter must always be removed by grinding and pickling. Remove weld discolouration by wire brushing and pickling with brushes.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><br />\n</div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><span style=\"color: #333333; font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\">Shipboard repairs:<o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><span style=\"color: #333333; font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\">Remember improper welding of ss by pretenders results in complete loss of the corrosion resistant properties. Do not burn ss while grinding. Use self sharpening grinding disc to avoid smearing. Ground area should be white and not blue/ brown. To prevent overheating the grinding disc must be constantly moved over a relatively large area ( use cooling air hose ) . The edges must blend in smooth without sharp edges and borders. If a rag is drawn and lint is shed the surface is too rough. When grinding remember the weld is harder than the ss plate. Always use matching electrode for molybdenum , chromium etc. Use small dia electrode, low heat input and matching amperage. To dry pits use very slight preheat. Minor pittings are ground. Use ss iron free zircon grinding disc of grain 80 ( coarse ) or 120 ( fine ). Zircon has a hardness of more than 8 on the Moh\u2019s scale.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><br />\n</div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><span style=\"color: #333333; font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\">Major pittings are drilled out like a valley ( the is to reach the bottom of the bulb ) and spot welded and then ground smooth. Never drill out pits as a blow hole on a spot weld is a corrosion initiator which will ooze black tatoo liquid once the non inert gas backed weld gets oxidised. Pittings start at 1 mm depth and dia. At times they are hidden with tiny entrance holes to a big cavity. Dye penetrant tests are useful when you know where to look for pittings. If you do not know where to look for pittings you will never find them. Small pittings are covered by a metal flap , but the subsurface bulb cavity may be quite large . The clad steel is only 2mm to 3mm thick on chemical tankers. If the clad steel pitting has breached through , first fill up with arc and then only with tig build up.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><br />\n</div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><span style=\"color: #333333; font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\">Any grinding must be followed by pickling and passivation. Cleaning before pickling must be done with strong warm non caustic alkaline detergent. Pickling burns iron particles and millscale. Every 12 deg rise in temperature halves the pickling time. All repair jobs such as welding, grinding etc., shall be pickled. Never pickle more than 30 minutes. Over-etching of stainless steel may produces coarse surfaces. Pickling contamination which would interfere with the passive oxide film of stainless steel. Pickling reduces pitting corrosion.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><br />\n</div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><span style=\"color: #333333; font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\">In welding SS with oxyacetylene it is necessary to use a tip which is 2 sizes smaller than a normal one used for mild steel. Since heat has a tendency to remain longer in the weld zone of SS a smaller flame reduces the possibility of destroying the properties of SS. A neutral flame is very essential for welding SS. Even a slightly oxidising flame oxidises the chrome in the SS thereby reducing its corrosion resistant qualities. Since it is difficult to maintain an exact neutral flame it is better to use a slight excess of acetylene.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><br />\n</div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><span style=\"color: #333333; font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\">Specially treated columbium filler rods are essential for good welding of SS. If SS rods are not available the second best way would be to cut strips from the mother metal and use them as filler rods. Not only does the chromium in the SS oxidise easily , but the oxide formed during welding acts as an insulating barrier between the flame and the workpiece. Success in welding ss therefore depends hugely on keeping heat to a minimum. Always use SS compatible flux and last but not the least complete the weld in one pass. You do not weave the low current small dia rod weld in SS tanks. Strike the arc on an arc striking plate and then lead the arc to the weld area. This is to make the welding current constant. Weld from edge to pit to other edge to avoid gas inside the pinhole bulb.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><br />\n</div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><span style=\"color: #333333; font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\">Welding rods for say 316L must have a carbon content of &lt;0.03 and a Mo content of&gt; 2.4. If the welding cable is too long, the voltage drop will be too great. If the cable is too small for the current it overheats and the power is lost.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><br />\n</div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><span style=\"color: #333333; font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\">It is commonplace for ageing parcel stainless steel chemical tankers to have on board a TIG welding set a MIG set and a plasma arc cutter. Of course every stainless steel shipyard will have them.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><br />\n</div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><span style=\"color: #333333; font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\">Tig stands for tungsten inert gas. The TIG electrode is non consumable. Inert gas prevents oxidation of electrode. For joints where additional weld metal is needed a filler rod is used.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><span style=\"color: #333333; font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\">It is important to have a weld that has the same properties as the base metal. Such a weld can only be made if the molten puddle is completely protected from the atmosphere, to prevent oxygen and nitrogen from being absorbed into the molten pool ( makes weld weak and porous ). No flux is required. Bonuses being very little smoke , fumes , sparks and weld spatter. If the amperage is &gt; 200 the ceramic cup at torch head is water cooled\u2014otherwise it is air cooled. Argon inert gas is heavier than air and blankets weld well. DC weld has pointed electrode and AC weld has spherical electrode. DC weld causes magnetised weld. In AC machine the electrode is not touched for starting the arc, unlike DC machine. The filler rod physical properties must be similar to the base metal. On light guage metals backing is used to protect the underside of the weld from atmospheric contamination. On heavier stock the copper backup bars draw the excess heat.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><br />\n</div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><span style=\"color: #333333; font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\">MIG stands for metallic inert gas. MIG set uses a continuous consumable wire electrode which is fed through the torch at preset controlled speeds. Less time is required to train an operator ( a couple of hours, to know the transfer type ). All the welder has to do is to pull the trigger and weld. As a rule weld failures are often due to the starting and stopping of welding\u2014since this includes slag, cold lapping and crater cracking. Spray transfer has constant spray of metal. In globular transfer the molten ball at the tip of electrode tends to grow 3 times the dia of wire before dropping down . In short cut transfer each drop touches the weld puddle before breaking away from the electrode wire. Electromagnetic force squeezes the drop from the wire. The short circuit is broken and the arc reignites. Shorting occurs 20 to 200 times per second. Shorting of arc pin points the effective heat. Intricate welds are thus possible. Argon, helium and Co2 gases are used for arc shielding austenitic stainless steel.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><span style=\"color: #333333; font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\">Generally surface porosity is the direct result of&nbsp;atmospheric&nbsp;contamination. The chief cause of crater defects is due to mindlessly removing the gun and shielding gas before the puddle has solidified.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><br />\n</div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><span style=\"color: #333333; font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\">Plasma arc cutting:<o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><span style=\"color: #333333; font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\">Temperatures up to a mind boggling 28000 deg C is possible. Plasma cutting is used in ship yards for high speed cutting of SS. Plasma is often considered the fourth state of matter. The other three being gas, liquid and solid. Plasma results when a gas is heated to a high temp and changes into positive ions , neutral atoms and negative electrons. When matter passes from one state to another latent heat is generated. Plasma torch supplies energy to a gas to change it to plasma. When plasma changes back to a gas heat is released. In a plasma arc torch the tip of the electrode is located within the nozzle which has a very small orifice. The gas emerges in the form of a supersonic jet hotter than any flame. It melts any known metal and its velocity blasts the molten metal through the kerf. When cutting SS best results are obtained with an Argon Hydrogen or Nitrogen Hydrogen gas mixture. Cooling water is used.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><br />\n</div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><span style=\"color: #333333; font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\">Plasma welding:<o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><span style=\"color: #333333; font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\">A central core of extreme temp surrounded by a sheath of cool gas. The required heat for fusion is generated by an electric arc which has been intensified by the injection of a gas into the arc stream. The superheated columnal arc is concentrated into a narrow stream. This when directed on metal makes possible penetrative welds without filler rods or edge preparation.so what is the big deal between tig and plasma welding? In plasma welding the arc column is constricted for higher heat. The arc plasma actually becomes a jet of high density current. The arc gas upon striking the metal cuts or keyholes entirely through the piece producing a small hole which is carried along the weld seam.during this cutting action the melted metal in front of the arc flows around the arc column then is immediately drawn together behind the hole by surface tension and reforms into a weld bead. A heavy duty DC rectifier is used as a source of power for plasma welding. Argon is used as plasma gas and helium as shielding gas ( argon too ).<o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><br />\n</div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><span style=\"color: #333333; font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\">Bottom line: fresh water rinsing of stainless steel tanks after tankcleaning with salt water must be doen by tankcleaning machine and not by hand hoses.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><br />\n</div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><span style=\"color: #333333; font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\">Some cargoes like Phosphoric acid and Sulphuric acid may form brown stains in the tanks and will not go with Nitric acid passivation or Metal brite. Such discolouration may be left as it is.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><br />\n</div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><span style=\"color: #333333; font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\">REMEMBER--Once the ship has been delivered , unless repairs have been done or contaminated with carbon steel or rusted by a very corrosive cargo--pickling is not necessary.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><span style=\"color: #333333; font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\">Know the temp of all chemicals to be loaded before accepting them on board.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><span style=\"color: #333333; font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\">Salt water at &gt;75deg c for &gt; 2hrs washing affects the SS. So after heated Palm oil Fatty acids, the SS layer gets affected.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><br />\n</div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><span style=\"color: #333333; font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\">When inspecting a SS tank use a magnifying glass, a good digital camera, a ladder and a good torch and chalk and a mirror. For cargoes requiring inert gas\u2014inspect the space above the cargo level.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><br />\n</div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><span style=\"color: #333333; font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\">Carriage of aggressive chemicals:--<o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><br />\n</div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><span style=\"color: #333333; font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\">Chlorinated HC must be stabilised so that no decomposition can occur. Temp must be less than 35C. the ppm of components must be less than<o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><span style=\"color: #333333; font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\">Water/ 100 ppm<o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><span style=\"color: #333333; font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\">Salt/ 15ppm<o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><span style=\"color: #333333; font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\">Hcl/ 15 ppm<o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><br />\n</div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><span style=\"color: #333333; font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\">For sodium hypochlorite solutions check the resistance tables for the carriage temp and the dilution strength. It cannot be carried on 316L and the clad steel will get holed during the voyage. 316LN, 317L and 317LN can handle the cargo<o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><br />\n</div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><span style=\"color: #333333; font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\">Allyl chloride at 20C pits 304L to 317L the same amount. 317LN is effected less.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><br />\n</div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><span style=\"color: #333333; font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\">Benzyl chloride and Benzene Sulphonyl Chloride at 20C pits 304L, 316L, 316LN, 317L, and 317LN almost the same.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><br />\n</div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><span style=\"color: #333333; font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\">Caustic potash must be carried less than 45 deg c and less than 50% dilution<o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><br />\n</div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><span style=\"color: #333333; font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\">Nitric acid of &gt;90 strength cannot be carried. Lesser strengths depend on carriage temp .<o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><span style=\"color: #333333; font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\">Eg\u2014<o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><span style=\"color: #333333; font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\">70% to 90% --max 50 deg c<o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><span style=\"color: #333333; font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\">&lt;70 %--max 70 deg c Sulfic acid\u2014 Must be &gt;96% and &lt;35 deg c<o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><br />\n</div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><span style=\"color: #333333; font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\">Sodium hydroxide solution, borohydride/ sodium hydroxide solution and potassium hydroxide solution must be less than 70% and 80 deg C<o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><br />\n</div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><span style=\"color: #333333; font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\">N-butyraldehyde, N-valeraldehyde and iso-valeraldehyde must be carried under inert gas padding.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><br />\n</div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><span style=\"color: #333333; font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\">The heavy oxides on the heat affected zone formed by a new weld repair can be removed by hydrofluoric acid pickling.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><span style=\"color: #333333; font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\">Nitric acid can both remove free iron and oxidize (passivate) the SS surface. It will not remove oxides.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><span style=\"color: #333333; font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\">Hydrogen peroxide can oxidize the SS surface but it cannot remove free iron to create the chromium rich layer that then oxidizes very readily in air to form the passive layer.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><span style=\"color: #333333; font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\">Citric acid passivation solutions can also get high chrome oxide ratios on the surface, and good resistance to corrosion .<o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><br />\n</div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;\"><span style=\"color: #333333; font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\">AND FINALLY-- Any repairs to SS tanks are only to be carried out after authorisation from us.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\"><a href=\"http://3.bp.blogspot.com/_tugjD0mUn6M/TQJApjG9iEI/AAAAAAAABo8/9LrMsjmjblc/s1600/ss3.JPG\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;\"><img border=\"0\" src=\"http://3.bp.blogspot.com/_tugjD0mUn6M/TQJApjG9iEI/AAAAAAAABo8/9LrMsjmjblc/s1600/ss3.JPG\" /></a></div><div style=\"line-height: 13.5pt; "POTASSIUM PERMANGANATE ON CHEMICAL TANKERS --  CAPT AJIT VADAKAYIL", "content": "<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><b style=\"mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 16pt;\">&nbsp;&nbsp; &nbsp; KMnO4-- &nbsp; &nbsp;<o:p></o:p></span></b></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\"><a href=\"http://4.bp.blogspot.com/_tugjD0mUn6M/TQEjB8w6t-I/AAAAAAAABoE/mcSO6HwYEvc/s1600/images+%25285%2529.jpg\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;\"><img border=\"0\" src=\"http://4.bp.blogspot.com/_tugjD0mUn6M/TQEjB8w6t-I/AAAAAAAABoE/mcSO6HwYEvc/s1600/images+%25285%2529.jpg\" /></a></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\">KMnO4 crystals exist as purple rhombic prisms. &nbsp;</span></div><div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\"><a href=\"http://1.bp.blogspot.com/_tugjD0mUn6M/TQEjQIE9MtI/AAAAAAAABoI/eJLYwEM_zPc/s1600/images+%25286%2529.jpg\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;\"><img border=\"0\" src=\"http://1.bp.blogspot.com/_tugjD0mUn6M/TQEjQIE9MtI/AAAAAAAABoI/eJLYwEM_zPc/s1600/images+%25286%2529.jpg\" /></a></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><br />\n</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"background-color: yellow;\">You must have 0.1 grammes of crystals pre measured in sealed glass tubes . &nbsp;Mix it with 500 CC water only when required to get the requisite 0.02% strength.</span> &nbsp;Even if kept in the fridge , once mixed-- the shelf life is just 3 days.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\">Potassium permanganate is flammable by chemical reaction, and is a powerful oxidiser which is spontaneously flammable on reaction with Ethylene Glycol, Glycerine, Acetone, Alcohols, Aluminium, Acids and Carbon.&nbsp; Explosion may occur, either when dry or in wet solution, in contact with organic or readily oxidisable materials. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\">It is moderately toxic by ingestion or subcutaneous route.&nbsp; It is used as an antibacterial agent.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><br />\n</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><b>Failure of PTT:---</b><o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\">The Potassium Permanganate test does not detect all types of contamination.&nbsp; It is common to obtain a good time on on the PTT and fail on water miscibility (hydrocarbon) test.&nbsp; Potassium permanganate does not react with hydrocarbons.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><br />\n</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\">PTT test fails only when contaminants react with KMNO4.&nbsp; PTT time can be increased by bleach or a chlorinated solvent. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\">The following lists indicates which type of products react with Potassium Permanganate and cause the PTT to fail.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><br />\n</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" matter:<o:p></o:p></span></i></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\">Lead<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\">Wood<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\">Ethylene glycol<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\">Acetic acid<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><i><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\">Violent reaction with:<o:p></o:p></span></i></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\">Acetone<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\">Tert-butylamine<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times serif;\"><o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><b>Recommended procedure:--</b><o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\">By spraying (recirc) the tank with Potassium Permanganate your tank will pass the PTT time (just by preempting the surveyors medium ).&nbsp; The tank has to be clean before spraying.&nbsp; Traces of the above mentioned chemicals will react to the Potassium Permanganate mix.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><br />\n</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\">The different ways of spraying Potassium Permanganate with good results are:<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\">1 &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Put one table spoon Permanganate in a 200 litre barrel.&nbsp; Use a spray gun and leave water running into the barrel while spraying as this mixture is strong.&nbsp; Spray tank for about 45-60 minutes.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\">2 &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Mix six table spoons of Potassium Permanganate crystals in 2 cum of water&nbsp; and recirc for half an hour. &nbsp;This method might take more time as it has to be repeated if the mix turns straw yellow too soon.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\">3 &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Steam the tank, inserting a strong mixture of Potassium Permanganate, for about 60 minutes.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\">In all cases the tank must be thoroughly washed afterwards to remove the Potassium Permanganate/sludge.&nbsp; There are no known coating restrictions.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><br />\n</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"background-color: yellow; font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\">WALL WASH:-</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><br />\n</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\">Indication of contamination will turn the Potassium Permanganate to a straw yellow colour.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><br />\n</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: left;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\">There are many notorious places in the world where the surveyor (with ulterior motives) comes on board with his own expired KMnO4 solution and fails the ship. &nbsp;In such a case mix your own solution .</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: left;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><br />\n</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: left;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\">Use 0.1 grams of crystals to 500 CC DI water to get 0.02% strength and run a test.</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: left;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><br />\n</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: left;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\">To prove the surveyors solution is expired , use pure lab Methanol and run a test . &nbsp;If this test does not run for 120 minutes , the surveyors solution is expired--- shelf life over or not kept in cool/ dark place.</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: left;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><br />\n</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: left;\"></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; margin-left: -6pt; margin-right: 25.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><i><span style=\"color: blue;\">Look down into tube kept in a cold 15C water bath of <span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"background-color: yellow;\">white colour in daylight or fluorescent tube light</span></span></i><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"background-color: yellow;\"><span style=\"color: blue;\">.</span>&nbsp;&nbsp;</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; margin-left: -6pt; margin-right: 25.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><br />\n</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; margin-left: -6pt; margin-right: 25.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\">Low PTT is often the result of a reducer remaining on the tank surface which could be the cargo itself.&nbsp;&nbsp;</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; margin-left: -6pt; margin-right: 25.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><br />\n</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; margin-left: -6pt; margin-right: 25.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\">Bleach is known to be contrary to a reducer and is an oxidising agent. Recirc at 50 deg after opening the pores of the coating.&nbsp;&nbsp;</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; margin-left: -6pt; margin-right: 25.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><br />\n</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; margin-left: -6pt; margin-right: 25.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\">Wash old PTT tested glass in HCL, then water and then Methanol.&nbsp;</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; margin-left: -6pt; margin-right: 25.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><i><span style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></i></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; margin-left: -6pt; margin-right: 25.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><i><span style=\"color: blue;\">The pinkish purple of the Potassium Permanganate solution changes to straw yellow ( Manganese di Oxide )</span></i>. Extreme of pH can interfere with test. Check every 5 minutes . PTT test detects all inhibited chemicals.&nbsp;&nbsp;</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; margin-left: -6pt; margin-right: 25.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><br />\n</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; margin-left: -6pt; margin-right: 25.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\">&nbsp;PTT test fails only when contaminants react with KMNO4.</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; margin-left: -6pt; margin-right: 25.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><br />\n</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; margin-left: -6pt; margin-right: 25.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\">HC does not react with KMNO4.&nbsp; So PTT time can be increased by Bleach or Chlorinated solvents . An equivalent of Stolt X is marketed by chemical companies too to neutralise the effects of Acrylic Monomers.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; margin-left: -6pt; margin-right: 25.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><br />\n</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; margin-left: -6pt; margin-right: 25.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\">To get the true color of the faded straw yellow a standard solution of platinum cobalt (Uranyl Nitrate ) is available in the market.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; margin-left: -6pt; margin-right: 25.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><br />\n</span></div><div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\"><a href=\"http://3.bp.blogspot.com/_tugjD0mUn6M/TQEi9wWLdZI/AAAAAAAABoA/PCRID5y8tqA/s1600/ptt_test_s4ad4694a18c0a.JPG\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;\"><img border=\"0\" height=\"240\" src=\"http://3.bp.blogspot.com/_tugjD0mUn6M/TQEi9wWLdZI/AAAAAAAABoA/PCRID5y8tqA/s320/ptt_test_s4ad4694a18c0a.JPG\" width=\"320\" /></a></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; margin-left: -6pt; margin-right: 25.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><br />\n</span></div><div class=\"TxBrp3\" style=\"line-height: normal; margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; margin-left: -6pt; margin-right: 25.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\">The Potassium permanganate solution should be stored in brown bottles and in the dark.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"TxBrp3\" style=\"line-height: normal; margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; margin-left: -6pt; margin-right: 25.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><br />\n</span></div><div class=\"TxBrp3\" style=\"line-height: normal; margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; margin-left: -6pt; margin-right: 25.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\">Even if the PTT test taken on board before arrival passed, gives no quarantee to have the same result from the surveyors test. (Different spots taken by surveyor).<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"TxBrp3\" style=\"line-height: normal; margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; margin-left: -6pt; margin-right: 25.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; margin-left: -6pt; margin-right: 25.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\">Glass apparatus that have a `brown film' should not be used as it is Manganese di-oxide, the reduced product of potassium permanganate. This will catalyse the oxidation/reduction decolorisation process of potassium permanganate and will give less PTT time. Glassware is cleaned by overnight immersion in an acid bath of 50% hydrochloric acid. The clean tubes must then rinsed well in tap water followed by DI water / Methanol.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoBodyTextIndent2\" style=\"margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; margin-left: -6pt; margin-right: 25.45pt; margin-top: 0in;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; margin-left: -6pt; margin-right: 25.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\">Similarly, the flask&nbsp; containing stock solution of potassium permanganate requires cleaning between batches of fresh solution. The last rinse should be with fresh potassium permanganate solution and not methanol.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; margin-left: -6pt; margin-right: 25.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; margin-left: -6pt; margin-right: 25.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\">Glass apparatus that have a `brown film' should not be used as it is Manganese di-oxide, the reduced product of potassium permanganate. This will catalyse the oxidation/reduction decolorisation process of potassium permanganate and will give less PTT time. Glassware is cleaned by overnight immersion in an acid bath of 50% hydrochloric acid. The clean tubes must then rinsed well in tap water followed by DI water / Methanol.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoBodyTextIndent2\" style=\"margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; margin-left: -6pt; margin-right: 25.45pt; margin-top: 0in;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; margin-left: -6pt; margin-right: 25.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\">Similarly, the flask&nbsp; containing stock solution of potassium permanganate requires cleaning between batches of fresh solution. The last rinse should be with fresh potassium permanganate solution and not methanol.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; margin-left: -6pt; margin-right: 25.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoBodyTextIndent2\" style=\"margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; margin-left: -6pt; margin-right: 25.45pt; margin-top: 0in;\"><span lang=\"EN-GB\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\">Uranyl nitrate is HIGHLY TOXIC. This substance must not come into contact with the skin and NEVER be pipetted by mouth. Treat the Uranyl nitrate/ Cobaltous chloride standard solution with care.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; margin-left: -6pt; margin-right: 25.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; margin-left: -6pt; margin-right: 25.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\">It is easy to fail this test if gasolene dye fillers / cutters&nbsp; or inhibitor chemical is present.</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; margin-left: -6pt; margin-right: 25.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; margin-left: -6pt; margin-right: 25.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><i><span style=\"color: blue;\">50cc filtered wash + 2cc KMNO4 ( 0.02 % strength )</span></i>.&nbsp; Mix 0.1 gms of the solid in tube to 500 cc of di water to get 0.02% strength.&nbsp; It takes 1.5&nbsp; hrs for the KMNO4 crystals to dissolve.</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; margin-left: -6pt; margin-right: 25.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><br />\n</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; margin-left: -6pt; margin-right: 25.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\">&nbsp;Keep in a dark place at 15C. <i><span style=\"color: blue;\">Note the time taken for the purple pink colour to change to straw yellow .&nbsp;&nbsp; Must hold for 50 minutes in the bath of 15C in a dark place.&nbsp; Check every 5 minutes</span></i>.&nbsp; <o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; margin-left: -6pt; margin-right: 25.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; margin-left: -6pt; margin-right: 25.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\">Use HCL, then DI water, then Methanol&nbsp; to wash glass , then water and finally Methanol.&nbsp;</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; margin-left: -6pt; margin-right: 25.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><br />\n</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; margin-left: -6pt; margin-right: 25.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\">Under&nbsp; the purest conditions KMNO4 test will run 120 min. If the bath is colder than 15C the test will run longer.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; margin-left: -6pt; margin-right: 25.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><br />\n</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; margin-left: -6pt; margin-right: 25.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\">For PTT 50 min at 15 deg C = 30 min at 20 deg C= 20 min at 28 deg C.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; margin-left: -6pt; margin-right: 25.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><br />\n</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; margin-left: -6pt; margin-right: 25.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\">Do PTT tests for all tanks at same time\u2014this way you know which tank is the best/ worst.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; margin-left: -6pt; margin-right: 25.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\"><a href=\"http://3.bp.blogspot.com/_tugjD0mUn6M/TQc4dVANRmI/AAAAAAAAB4I/XZoaNzsE7No/s1600/capt+ajit+vadakayil.JPG\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em;
